B00EW9GQR6|4.0|Artpop, above all else, is a continuation in Lady Gaga's exploration of her usual themes: artifice as personal expression, modern sexuality, and the effects of worldwide fame. I think it's great.<br /><br />Lady Gaga is as intelligent as she is totally bonkers. Artpop is expansive and sprawling, and seems like a bit of a mess at first glance, but its barrage of hooks and melodies works in its favor. Much like Born This Way, it's got so much ear candy that, even if you get lost in all its twists and turns, it's a fun place to explore.<br /><br />Gaga said at one point that she'd like to perform this album in its entirety, so she wisely constructs it in a way that would work for a live show, starting strong, pacing the album well, and closing with the two best songs: Gypsy, a gorgeous melody with some of her best lyrics, a pure pop number that has much in common with the classic song of the same title by Fleetwood Mac; and Applause, which would be a powerful encore in any show.<br /><br />She's a big personality, and much of her strength comes from that (note the various self-referential lines that call back to her earlier songs). The guest stars never overwhelm her, though they are given room to shine. This is definitely Gaga's show, and she makes the most of it. From the pulsing electronic music to the pure pop to the ballad, Dope, the artist is in fine form.<br /><br />There are high expectations of Lady Gaga, and people will no doubt criticize this album for not taking things to even greater extremes or varying enough from her previous themes, but Lady Gaga has created an outstanding pop album that moves her sound forward, if incrementally, and has plenty of interesting bits to keep us tuned in for quite some time.

B00EW9GQR6|5.0|Lady Gaga keeps the momentum going strong on her adventurous roller coaster of a third album. \\"ARTPOP\\" is a giddy, swirling, unfailingly intriguing look through her singular and ever-surprising mind. It is often clever, sometimes eyebrow-raising and always entertaining - descriptions which befit the songstress herself.<br /><br />Rather than simply deliver a collection of chart-aimed retreads of past pop-savvy hits (no one would complain to hear a \\"Poker Face\\" or \\"Love Game\\" soundalike, since those tunes were so strong) Gaga channels her inner Tori Amos for the better part of the album, allowing for an album defined more by eccentricity and insularity than accessibility, even though the likes of \\"Gypsy\\" or previous hits \\"Applause\\" and \\"Do What U Want,\\" both strong indicators of the LP as a whole, are not without strong hooks and radio friendly rhythms.<br /><br />Her declaration of wanting to craft \\"reverse Warhol\\" art with \\"ARTPOP\\" certainly works in that she has designed the album to reach the listener from its surface energy - this is music that makes a blaring, willfully garish, neon-lighted impression on the listener but ultimately leaves her exact intent up to interpretation. Just how tongue-in-cheek are these messages? How much is sarcasm? How much is parody? One thing is certain - Gaga set out to make a record that would get people talking, and she succeeded.<br /><br />Although this is an album more about overall feel than individual moments, \\"Venus\\" and \\"Sexxx Dreams\\" are riper than most of the bunch to arrest clubbers on the dance floor, and \\"Gypsy\\" and \\"G.U.Y.\\" are single material with hooks-a-plenty construction and compelling performances. \\"Swine\\" is giddy fun, the title track is cheeky and slinky with its retro 80s synths, and \\"Dope,\\" written as a repentance from a damaged, downtrodden addict, is a surprisingly powerful ballad. Gaga's cocktail hour vocal is honest and heartfelt.<br /><br />So much is outwardly crass and openly superficial - that is, so 2013 - about \\"ARTPOP,\\" and that appears to be Gaga's superobjective, a writhe commentary in and of itself - as she continually channels her inner Marie Antoinette, hedonistic pleasures battling each other to get to the threshold, she has her cake and eats it, too. B00BATG18K|5.0|Amy Tan is a master of character development and a master story teller, and in her latest historical fiction novel, The Valley of Amazement, she takes these skills to new heights while bridging the gap between western and Asian culture, placing her in the realm of artists like Dostoyevsky, Tolstoy, Joyce, and Faulkner.<br /><br />No author paints the psychological struggle between strong willed mother/daughter pairs better than Tan, and the story unfolds between a privileged Chinese-American girl, Violet, and her American mother, Lucia, who operates a first class courtesan house in old Shanghai during the fall of the Ching Dynasty.  Lucia is cruelly deceived by one of her lovers and confidants who sells fourteen-year-old Violet to a second rate courtesan house as Lucia, thinking Violet is already on board, boards a ship for San Francisco to escape the political turmoil of the era.<br /><br />The story covers both Violet and Lucia and examines their lives in minute detail, particularly focusing on the choices they make concerning their mothers and all the men in their lives.<br /><br />Unlike her other novels, Tan fully develops the sexual nature of her main characters in this book, which adds to the psychological richness of the story.  Her strong point is the creation of characters, so real, so believable, so human, that the reader will feel as if she knows these people--the mark of a great writer.<br /><br />This is the pinnacle work of Amy Tan to date, and it is a journey all serious readers should take.

B00GBCMW9S|3.0|It's interesting to read the wildly differing opinions on Eminem's newest effort The Marshall Mathers LP 2.  Newsday believes that the album doesn't work as its intended sequel to 2000's The Marshall Mathers LP.  The Daily Beast treats it as nothing more than a reminder of the fact that Em has done better work, and that this isn't it.  Entertainment Weekly also wasn't thrilled with the album, giving it a C+ overall.<br /><br />But hey, NPR has Em's back (for the most part), and that should tell you something.  And Rolling Stone likes it...I think.  Once these two judges are holding up their 8.0 cards, there's really no need to check in with anyone else.<br /><br />Eminem is such a lyrical genius that to even attempt to review his work is intimidating.  If this was the end of \\"8 Mile\\" and we saw him standing there, we'd just drop the mic and leave with our tails between our legs.<br /><br />That being said, let's attempt to dissect The Marshall Mathers LP 2.  First, it has to be said: the title hurts the album.  Sequels naturally lend themselves to being vulnerable as comparisons to their predecessors, and Eminem has progressed so strongly and consistently in the years post-The Marshall Mathers LP (with the exception of the slight hiccup that was 2009's Relapse, which was quickly rectified [and apologized for] via the appropriately-named Recovery in 2010) that for him to tie new material to a 2000 album seems like he's doing himself a disservice.  (Did we really need a sequel to \\"Stan\\"?)<br /><br />The Marshall Mathers LP was brilliant.  It was here that we began to take Eminem more seriously as an artist, as opposed to just a naughty cartoon animated by Dr. Dre.  Here, we had an updated Beastie Boy - a white-boy rapper who was easy on the eyes and who could hold his own when the odds were clearly not in his favor.  The problem is that because LP was so innovative, its sequel could only suffer by comparison.<br /><br />Recovery is arguably Eminem's best album of all time.  It featured Em's killer collaborations with artists like P!nk and Rihanna, and it was brutally honest without making the listener uncomfortable - a delicate balance that Em doesn't always strike so perfectly, and that he often misses here.<br /><br />For one thing, in light of the recent strides same-sex marriage has made in the years since Recovery's release, people are less open to Em's choice of words when he continues to add \\"fa**ot\\" to his lyrics.  Em has defended his use of the word in that it isn't meant as a derogatory term for a sexual preference, but people don't want to hear it.  They believe that it's hateful, outdated, and unnecessary.<br /><br />While these folks may find Em to be stagnant, he actually shows emotional growth at several points on this album.  \\"Headlights\\" is especially surprising, as Em takes this opportunity to apologize to his mother, Debbie Mathers, for ripping her a new one so publicly in the past.  Apparently, he regrets writing \\"Cleaning Out My Closet\\" and won't even play it in concert anymore.  This is disappointing, as I was one proud college freshman the day my mom told me she liked that song - oh, the irony.<br /><br />When Em becomes reflective, it feels bittersweet.  You're proud of him for overcoming his demons but at the same time, if you haven't yet overcome your own, you're sad that he can no longer relate to yours.  It's sobering to hear him rap about his doubts as to whether or not he was ever meant to be a father, since all we've heard him do for years is defend his girls to the death.<br /><br />Em's samples of The Zombies' \\"Time of the Season\\" (\\"Rhyme or Reason\\") and Billy Squier's \\"The Stroke\\" (\\"Berzerk\\") need multiple listens for a determination of whether or not they work.  Em's samplings aren't usually this tough to follow.  \\"Survival\\" (a.k.a. the \\"Call of Duty\\" track) kicks ass, but I am partial to his arena rap-rock.  Missing from many of these songs is Em's familiar acid-spitting, though when he does bring his old ire out to play on songs like \\"Rap God\\" or \\"Berzerk,\\" it feels less like he's rallying the troops and more like he's trying to prove he's still got it.<br /><br />The problem is that The Marshall Mathers LP 2 delves even deeper into the remorseful ditch that Recovery had already started digging.  Eminem feels less like that ticking time bomb who's destined to sit in the back of a police car and more like the ex-con who feels contrition for the actions that put him there.ring his old ire out to play on songs like \\"Rap God\\" or \\"Berzerk,\\" it feels less like he's rallying the troops and more like he's trying to prove he's still got it.<br /><br />The problem is that The Marshall Mathers LP 2 delves even deeper into the remorseful ditch that Recovery had already started digging.  Eminem feels less like that ticking time bomb who's destined to sit in the back of a police car and more like the ex-con who feels contrition for the actions that put him there.

B00DR0PDNE|5.0|It's been a very popular aspect of our semi-weekly board game night. Sometimes between turns someone will play a video from Youtube just for fun, and it makes for a pretty good addition for the night. Otherwise, my wife and I like to use it to watch content from Netflix as well. It works very well as advertised, so long as you understand that going outside of what's advertised isn't guaranteed to work as well as you might like.<br /><br />The device itself does not have any sort of permanent memory for apps, instead it loads them on demand, usually taking about 3 to 5 seconds to load the Netflix or Youtube apps. It can cause some hiccups and glitches if you try to load a video while it's downloading the app, but otherwise works very smoothly if you allow it those few seconds at first. The device itself streams content directly from those sites, so you can queue up content from low end devices without any playback problems.<br /><br />The desktop casting does leave much to be desired, and I haven't been able to get the audio to work; though, it's not an advertised feature and is clearly marked as experimental. The Tab-Casting on the other hand works great, given you have a good enough computer to handle streaming content smoothly (we have a computer that we built for about $1,000 last year, works great on that. Our other computer would probably be worth about $350 today, and it stutters with video and audio gets out of sync). The Tab-Casting feature allows you to play anything you can open in your browser on your television, at least, we haven't run into anything that causes problems thus far. If you have the proper plugins, this will allow you to play video content from your computer and stream it to your television, or any number of creative ideas you might have.<br /><br />The Youtube app works well from all of the devices our friends have: Android phones, iPad, Laptops/Desktops (Linux and Windows). We haven't tried it from anything else, but I imagine they work just as well. You can queue videos from several devices and the Chromecast will play them in the order they were requested in. This means that you and your friends can add videos to a playlist as someone else's video is playing. One thing to keep in mind, once Youtube on your device syncs up with the Chromecast, it will display controls for the current video on your device, sometimes causing people to accidentally queue the current video up again or restart it from the beginning. It's mostly corrected if you give it a few seconds to get situated and make sure you're actually doing what you think you're doing.<br /><br />The Netflix app is similar to the Youtube app, though it does not have a queue. It does have a few more issues, though I believe those are mostly related to the fact that the Netflix app for phones is a resource hog, it works great once you can actually send the video request to the Chromecast device. So it's not really an issue with the Chromecast itself, but with the Netflix app on your phone. There is only a slight latency (less than 1 second unless you're having network issues) with the controls for a playing video, though it can be irritating to try to get the controls to come back up if you close out of the netflix app, once again, an issue with the Netflix app on your phone.<br /><br />I don't buy music or videos from the Google Play store, so I haven't tested that out. I imagine it works well.<br /><br />As far as I know, anyone can make an app for the device to play content. However, I would warn people from making a purchase based on future promises from other content providers. Until they actually have an app, you should consider it to be nothing more than a possibility. The Tab-Casting can make up for an app not being available, but having a Chromecast app is superior.<br /><br />Overall, I've been very happy with the device. It works very well as advertised, and the price is appropriate for what it is.ust as well. 1400069289|4.0|The Power of Habit by Charles Duhigg is an engaging read that examines the human machinery behind our habits. Underlying our actions are behavior patterns that have grown over time through the way our mind makes associations. In 1892, William James, the famous philosopher/ psychologist, said that our life is but a mass of habits. And in 21st Century, Mr. Duhigg, with in-depth illustrations and a simple model, teaches us how the habits function through cues, behavior patterns, and rewards.<br /><br />The book is both theoretical and practical. Mr. Duhigg covers the power of habits from many angles (ethics, influencing forces, learning, neurology, and business, etc.), and sharply concludes that we can change our habits. If you coach people, help lead change, or are trying hard to improve your own effectiveness, then I highly recommend this book.<br /><br />To be balanced, I think too much time is spent on looking at legal cases and ethical concerns. The core information may be gleaned early into the book. However, through the extensive and diverse examples, Mr. Duhigg reinforces the central message that our habits are indeed powerful, but can be shaped to achieve the rewards you truly want.

B0036S4B6M|2.0|After watching Season 1 of Orange Is The New Black and enjoying it, I am extremely disappointed by this book. It's very rare that a TV show or movie is better than a book, but this is one of those cases. Everything that makes the TV show good is missing from the book. In the memoir, Kerman has a bad habit of explaining rather than showing when it's something important: She pontificates generally about the sad state of the criminal justice system, but she doesn't give other prisoners' vignettes the way they do in the TV show. The result is that all the characters come off as less interesting and the story is less compelling. Interestingly, Kerman does expend the effort to show rather than explain when it's a matter that is relatively unimportant to the story: She spends pages and pages describing foods she ate or how they went about decorating the jail for various holidays. These details don't drive a story.<br /><br />Also, there's so much in the TV show that is missing from the book, but not much in the book that's not in the TV show. After going to jail, Kerman's lesbian codefendant doesn't reappear until 90% into the book, and the real story isn't nearly as interesting as the TV show. If you, like me, are buying this book because you enjoyed the TV show, be warned that they are very different and that the book is much less interesting.

I think if this track and one or two others were left off, this would have been a perfect album.<br /><br />The remaining half of the album includes production from french house producers Zedd and David Guetta along with Leqlercq and will.i.am:<br /><br />1. Fashion! - This funky track sounds like a merging of Daft Punk's Get Lucky, Madonna's Holiday, and David Bowie's Let's Dance and just makes me want to move.  This is a David Guetta/will.i.am production and for the most part is pop perfection.  The problem for me is the last 40 seconds kind of get too hectic and kill the groove.  Nonetheless, I absolutely love this track.<br />2. Donatella - This beat is so fierce and strong with a diva-esque fashiony comedic alter ego with comicy lyrics to go along with what is a surefire club banger. This Zedd production needs to be released asap!<br />3. Gypsy - Produced by Leclercq, this is the \\"Edge of Glory\\" on this album and should be the next single.<br />4. G.U.Y. - Guy Under You is another excellent Zedd production with a great beat to dance to.<br />5. Dope - This is the only ballad on this album and is just stunning.  Based on the strength of the other songs on this album I am not sure I support this one being a single but based on indicators when it was released as a promo, it may do well.<br />6. Aura - Strong fresh electronic opener.  There's a demo floating around that some gaga fans prefer over the final released version.  It may be worth searching the web to hear what you think.<br />7. Venus - While I love the beat of this track, I am just not a fan of the lyrics.<br />8. Mary Jane Holland - is one of the very few track on the album which I skip.<br /><br />Long story short, Lady Gaga has put out an album of 15 tracks with minimal fillers and a strong number of potential number one singles.  If you want a fantastic electronic album to dance to, this is the one.  She exudes confidence, pokes fun at herself and pop culture while infusing today's electro edm beats as her back-drop.ctro edm beats as her back-drop.

1451620829|5.0|I have not recently enjoyed a book by a rock icon as much as this one, perhaps because it was told by the Catman, himself.  \\"Makeup to Breakup\\" is an excellent chronological narration by Peter Criss about his entire life: growing up on the streets of Brooklyn, playing the local bars, achieving superstardom in KISS,  post-KISS life.....to present day.<br /><br />One of the main things that appealed to me about the style of this book is that the author made me feel as though I was sitting down, having a few beers with him while he told this story. Another is that Peter is a local guy from Brooklyn who, along with the other members of KISS, had an astounding impact on rock in the 70s. When I was growing up, there wasn't one teen I knew that didn't idolize the band members in KISS. While they weren't the greatest of musicians, KISS brought an excitement to the stage of rock 'n roll that no other band did, at the time. In fact, I recall from having seen them at Madison Square Garden, exactly what Peter said about the early days of KISS:  the band was so loud that it was probably 20 seconds into every song before I knew which one was playing. My ears were ringing for the next day after that....<br /><br />Another reason that I liked this book so much is that at least Peter came clean about his years as an alcoholic/drug addict.  He didn't try to hide behind anything or lie about it....He admitted it and saw it as a problem. Now, as many that have seen Peter as a \\"megalomaniac\\", I just didn't see the same thing and maybe because I am being impartial as a reviewer. I have not been a KISS fan since my youth, but I can still acknowledge that Mr. Criss has crafted a well-written, candid account of his life and it was well-worth reading. In fact, Peter is a very funny author and numerous times, I found myself laughing out loud at his dialogue, his depiction of the KISS life backstage and stories of other KISS band members. In addition, I acknowledge the  innovation, theatrics and stage presence that KISS brought to the world of rock.<br /><br />I had read one of Gene Simmons' books several years back and I liked it, but not as much as this. Yes, it's clear that Gene is a highly talented, creative businessman that had dynamic visions of stardom from the start. One thing that definitely parallels between Gene/Peter's books is that Gene and Paul always controlled KISS and Ace and Peter were made less significant. As Gene mentions, Ace and Peter never really held jobs in the early days of KISS (nor were they sober enough) and it was left up Gene/Paul to provide the finances. In addition, it was really Gene and Paul's band, anyway, since Peter and Ace later answered the ads placed, seeking musicians. Almost from the start, Peter was doomed to get a lesser share, percentage-wise, from that point forward.  It would never be his band, equally.<br /><br />There is a very good insight into the KISS animosity towards each other that Peter sheds a light on in this book.  I would tend to lean towards Peter's account of being mistreated or not treated as an equal......and that Gene and Paul were not the easiest to get along with. In fact, I would tend to see Gene and Paul as being on the arrogant side of things when it comes to many things:  I heard an interview with Gene in which he bashed Peter's drumming in the early days.  Frankly, Gene was not the best bass player or musician either, so he had nerve to criticize someone else.<br /><br />If you're looking for a very good book, written by a down-to-earth rock legend, this is it.nd stage presence that KISS brought to the world of rock.<br /><br />I had read one of Gene Simmons' books several years back and I liked it, but not as much as this. B00EEPFLHE|5.0|This album is what I would have expected from Stryper years ago.  While other efforts, ('Reborn', 'Murder By Pride', etc.), weren't without their high points; this CD is strong from start to finish.  As a whole, this is probably the 'hardest', or 'most metal' CD Stryper has ever put out.  It has more of an edge to it than their 80's stuff, (likely because it lacks the over-production so typical in the 'hair band' days); but is on-par with what you'd expect from Stryper.  Good guitars, strong vocals, signature Robert Sweet drums and a message that, while it doesn't beat you over the head, also refuses to be ignored or watered-down.  Rather than calling listeners to be 'Free' to make choices, or having ballads that could be taken as sung to God, or a significant other or a friend, this CD's message states that a Revelation is coming - things will be revealed, battles will take place, and that the truth is the truth and you have to deal with it.  Every song on this CD is good.  Unlike the last couple of studio CDs, (excluding \\"The Covering\\" - a CD of cover tunes, and \\"Second Coming\\" - a CD of re-recordings of old Stryper songs), I don't have to pick and choose songs to listen to.  The whole thing is good.  The whole thing ROCKS.<br />Oh, and I'm also a big fan of the artwork on the cover!  It's something I liked about the original release of \\"To Hell With The Devil\\" and about albums in general; and in this digital age, it's refreshing to see a CD cover tell a story and be worthy of hanging on a wall.  Even the photo on the back is cool.  It shows the guys - now - wearing the old outfits and in the same pose as what was on the back of the \\"To Hell With The Devil\\" album in 1986.  I think that shows their sense of humor and I happen to LOVE IT.  This album is a winner from start to finish.  Musically AND visually!<br /><br />I bought the CD/DVD Deluxe edition and it's good to have a couple of videos for the new songs at my fingertips with the DVD.  The only thing I wouldhave liked to see different in regards to the music videos, would maybe be to have a couple of the older videos on there, as well...just as a bonus/treat for us long-time fans.  Hopefully they come out with a video collection on DVD, (maybe with a live video recorded - for a change - in the U.S.).<br />What I would've liked to see in regards to the 'making of' video feature, would've been to maybe have the whole group sitting together and answering questions and giving commentary.  Instead, we get Michael Sweet making comments about each track on the CD and then there are a few short comments from the other guys peppered in.  It seems very heavy on Michael's views.  I'd have liked to see them all in one room, all giving their thoughts about each track and putting the CD together and what they hope going forward.  But, hey...it's a short 'making of' and two videos; and it's not why I bought it.  I bought it for the CD and this CD is a winner from start to finish!

B00F8L2VO4|5.0|In a nutshell, I would recommend this app to anyone wanting to learn a second language! The languages available to learn are Spanish, German, French, Portuguese, and Italian.<br /><br />After two weeks of using this app (in conjunction with an Italian workbook), I have advanced rapidly into learning the Italian language! I tried several other apps (and podcasts, too!) to learn Italian before I discovered this one. When it comes to learning for free, not one of the other apps or podcasts came close to being as useful and fast as Duolingo! I appreciate that I am learning some simple sentence structure rather than only vocab words. I like the variety of learning drills. Translate written sentences from Italian to English and vice versa, listen to Italian being spoken and write out in Italian what was said, translate by picking from a selection of words, and learning new nouns by choosing the right picture.<br /><br />One thing I'd like to  mention is that it may be useful to do some study of verb conjugation on your own to avoid some confusion while learning from Duolingo. This app does not walk you through boring verb conjugations; instead you are meant to pick them up as you progress. The good side to this is no boring verb conjugation drills or charts to slog through! The downside is that not knowing a little about verbs ahead of time may add frustration to your Duolingo learning experience.<br /><br />I believe there is no better way currently to learn a new language for free! Great app!

B000059XUP|2.0|Coming off the original Crow film, a cult classic in which its star Brandon Lee died in a tragic on-set accident, The Crow: City of Angels had its work cut out for it. Where do you go from there?<br /><br />The Crow: City of Angels (not to be confused with the Nicolas Cage/Meg Ryan drama City of Angels that was released a couple years later) takes the Crow story out of the darkly stylized pseudo-Detroit to a smoggy stylized pseudo-Los Angeles. Taking place at least 10 years after the original film, an adult Sarah (this time played by Mia Kirschner) has moved to L.A. and become a tattoo artist, but is plagued by dreams of the second arrival of The Crow.<br /><br />But instead of Eric Draven, we get Ashe Corven (Vincent Perez), a mechanic who is resurrected from the dead with the gift of invulnerability after being killed alongside his young son by a gang headed by the local druglord Judah Earl (Richard Brooks). Judah's gang is comprised of Spider Monkey (Vincent Castellanos), Nemo (a young Thomas Jane), Kali (Thuy Trang of Power Rangers fame), and Curve (rockstar Iggy Pop). Ashe sets out to take murderous vengeance against the gang, hunting them down one by one, hoping he'll be reunited with his son's spirit in the afterlife when he's finished. But things become complicated when Ashe and Sarah fall in love, and Judah discovers Ashe's one weakness.<br /><br />So first, the good things about the film: the production design. The film looks great. This polluted, smog-covered L.A. seems like its constantly cast in an jaundiced light, like the whole city is dying of liver failure from all the drugs and decadence its denizens feed itself. Its walls are covered in graffitti, its streets are littered with trash, and any sane person with enough sense would've left for another city long ago (I wonder what a Crow-ized pseudo Seattle or San Francisco would look like, but they're probably just as corrupt and polluted). The first film used Halloween and the night before, Devil's Night, as a backdrop for Eric Draven's story. But this film uses the Day of the Dead (Dio de los Muertos) in a similar way, as both celebrations share similarities. And the film make Day of the Dead look like a pretty cool party that should be observed more often outside of Mexico and L.A.<br /><br />But aside from those bright spots, the film is just not very good. Unfortunately, with a story like The Crow, you often have to follow the same story beats, making the film feel derivative and uninspired. Man gets killed, a loved one is also killed in the process, man returns from the dead, man hunts down and kills his murderers one by one. Lather, rinse, repeat with each sequel. Don't believe me? Also check out The Crow: Salvation. I haven't seen The Crow: Wicked Prayer, but I'm probably not going out on a limb and assuming it's no different. But how else would movie producers attempt to recapture the success of the first film without its star? By rehashing the same story over, and over, and over, and over. This film does attempt a more melancholy tone, but it results in a film feels more slow and plodding. The film's finale feels as butchered as it actually is. The original ending forced Ashe to choose between Sarah and his son, and it's a decision that ultimately leaves him without both of them in the end. However, studio interference led to cuts that removed that choice from the plot, leaving the film with a sense of stiltedness and unresolved ambiguity.<br /><br />City of Angels' script doesn't fare much better. Written by David Goyer (yes, of The Dark Knight Trilogy), the dialogue is somber and vaguely spiritual at times, repetitive at others. Ashe often repeats the last things each gang member said to him before they killed him. It's meant to be ironic, but it becomes stale and predictable really fast.<br /><br />Vincent Perez is miscast as Ashe. Half the time, his dialogue is barely intelligible underneath his thick accent. And I can't even tell what kind of accent it is. Is it French? Is it Italian? Is it Spanish? Where is Ashe supposed to be from? Whatever the case, you can't make out what he's saying. And as for his acting...well, yeah. He doesn't feel very menacing, and he has baffling moments of overacting that are downright comical. There is a scene where he trashes his garage amidst flashbacks of his son, and all it amounts to is a lot of yelling, kicking shelves, and knocking things down. I've seen just about the same amount of genuine emotion in Tommy Wiseau's attempts at angst in The Room, and I can't help but chuckle now.<br /><br />The rest of the cast fills out their parts no better, aside from Iggy Pop. At least Curve comes off sufficiently creepy. Richard Brooks' line delivery feels more like he's reading from a children's book instead of a script. Mia Kirschner's Sarah just doesn't seem to have much of a personality aside from being mopey and doe-eyed. Thuy Trang doesn't even seem like she can handle the film's violent content. It's like she's holding back, and not out of an actor's artistic restraint but because she really doesn't wanna be there.<br /><br />The film's music is decent if not very memorable. There's an ethereal orchestral score, but no particular theme that feels iconic. The film uses the occasional source music, with songs from the likes of Hole, PJ Harvey, Filter, and yes, an Iggy Pop song made the cut. Rock band The Deftones makes an appearance at the Day of the Dead celebration. This film tries to present us with a soundtrack to match the first film's impressive music, but like most of the film as a whole, it too falls short of those lofty ambitions.<br /><br />And that's ultimately what this film is, an attempt to capture the first film's success but a disappointing failure that makes you kinda wish they didn't try.

B006ZJJ6XW|5.0|While the performances here range from average to outstanding, I give this 5 stars since it's inexpensive and allows you to pick up some really great recordings of Nos. 7-9 (1 and 2 are good too, but I listen to them much less). Speaking of Toscanini, as other reviewers here have, the 8th is very much in his mold, with similar tempos and high drama in the outer movements (why everyone refers to this as a \\"genial\\" symphony I'm not sure, at least not based on the outer movements). Dynamic, propulsive, dramatic, beautiful--outstanding. The 7th is the same, and seems to have been recorded even better, with fresh, open sound. After an exciting introduction to the first movement, Leinsdorf's development continues at a slightly more moderate pace, yet there is still a palpable sense of excitement in the playing. Unusually for the time, he takes the repeats in the final movement, and his finely judged tempos and phrasing throughout make this also a standout 7th. Leinsdorf handles the opening of the 4th symphony a bit oddly, rushing the lead-in to the movement proper, which for me doesn't work, though I recall the final movement as as being especially pleasing. The 3rd strikes me as possibly the dullest in this set.<br /><br />I'm not certain this new remastering is better than the previous releases, which had lustrous strings and good ambiance. These sound different, and probably no worse, but not necessarily better.

B00F3VOL38|3.0|This issue, along with the volume from 1994,(which is much richer material-wise) give us probably the best chance to hear what the lads were really like as a post-Hamburg, polished, huge act. One of the bad raps that the guys always got was they were a mediocre LIVE band. The BBC Sessions prove that they were just exactly what John and Paul said- \\"a good little r'n'r band that made it very, very big...J Lennon, 1969.<br /><br />As far as the actual PRODUCT REVIEW, the sound is well mixed, with the guitars very clean and separated properly. John's chunk-chonk rhythm and George's leads and fills equally distinguishable.  Ringo's drum kit, especially the oft-overlooked kick drum, are dangled in just the proper places, with hi-hat sharpness very edgy and up in the mix, as it should be. Ringo was the heartbeat of this monster, by the way. Of course, Paul's bass gets good treatment.<br /><br />So I agree with a fellow reviewer that the lack of new, unheard Beeb songs brings this a 3.5 star review. Obviously, the historical aspect is cool, and the most enjoyable parts are the witty banter between BBC DJ's Muff and Matthews and the band, and their early day shout outs to individual fans and party situations for fans. That would quickly end as this group went atomic, which is an analogy I give to watching the group at the Cavern Club in 1962, it would be like standing next to a nuclear explosion. There are no new versions of songs, but the performances do prove that the band was competent performing live, and that George could produce a guitar solo on the spot, which has been often disputed. Go get em Georgie, and Johnny and Ritchie and Paul-thanks for the music dudes. We Love You...

B008ZDC7M8|4.0|'Tis said that the worst sin committed by any movie reviewer is to describe the movie that he or she would have made instead.  How-some-ever, I can think of no better way to critique Mark Cousins' intriguing \\"The Story of Film: An Odyssey\\" than by dragging him to the woodshed to teach the teacher a leson.  \\"Intriguing\\" because Cousins comes tantalizingly close to getting it right, but the misses are so woefully wide the mark as to put most viewers off...which is a tragedy because his insights are mostly so precise and so illuminating as to explain the very core of why the world is forever in the thrall of the medium (the cliche of \\"the stuff dreams are made of\\" to the contrary notwithstanding).<br /><br />So, first off, the music has to go.  It is loudly percussive and serves no other purpose than to annoy the viewer.<br /><br />Second, Cousins apparently dragged some talentless cinematographer around the world with him to film the historical locations to illustrate that which he's talking about.  These consist mostly of street scenes shot Andy Warhol-style with no apparent regard for content.  The shots are badly framed (wide-angle shots are best composed with the camera level and not pointed at the sky unless there's a plane up there that we're supposed to notice) and consist of little more than contemporary traffic whizzing by in the foreground...which makes no sense when Cousins is describing a 19th century film.  The only present-day shots that make any sense are those of filmmakers whom Cousins is interviewing.  That is, if no footage of \\"The Battleship Potemkin\\" is available, I would a lot rather see a 1925 postcard than a desultory steet scene of today's Odessa.<br /><br />Thirdly, I wish the supers would identify not only the movies they are imposed upon, but whetever else might be in the background (personalities, studios, equipment, memorabilia, posters, scenery).  Photoplays themselves may not be enhanced by explanations, but a \\"course\\" in film history can only benefit from a surfeit of pertinent information.<br /><br />Finally, Cousins has tried to stuff his arbitrary divisions of film history into a Procrustian bed of 15 more-or-less decades of different schemata (such as the unwieldy \\"Japanese Classicism and Hollywood Romance, 1928-1945\\") which are about as comfortable as a left shoe on a right foot.  If I were Cousins, I would have divided movie history into more universally recognized themes (chapters on \\"Film Noir,\\" \\"Westerns,\\" \\"Science Fiction,\\" \\"Romance,\\" \\"Buddy Films,\\" \\"Musicals,\\" \\"Mysteries,\\" \\"War Movies,\\" \\"Comedies,\\" \\"Costume Dramas,\\" etc.).  But, alas, Cousins seems to have lost my number.<br /><br />I would normally have written off such a lumpy effort with two or three stars, but I think \\"The Story of Film\\" deserves four stars...and not just for his effort (which is epic in its scope).  Cousins utters some of the most interesting things I have ever heard about individual directors and individual films (he seems to have little use for process or technique; he describes most shots where the camera moves as \\"tracking\\" shots, whether or not it is a pan, arm, tilt, crane or steadicam).  Definitely worth a look-see.  If you don't want to commit to the fancy boxed edition, the whole shebang is currently available on Netflix.  (And then there's Cousins' book of the same name available from Amazon - advt.)<br /><br />Some commentators have disapproved of Cousins' lilting Irish accent (and the fact that he often talks over the dialog of the shot he's describing), but I find his voice charming and natural.  If he taught a course at USC or UCLA, I would be there in a heartbeat.

They seemed to \\"all over the place\\", and Pendergast was painted with a comic book super hero paintbrush.<br /><br />White Fire is a masterfully constructed tale with all the action, tight squeezes, and plot twists that you expect from Mr. Preston and Mr. Child. Much of the story takes place from the point of view of Corrie Swanson, Pendergast's young prot&eacute;g&eacute;e, who is working on a thesis project. She gets a few helpful pokes from Pendergast, but moves most of the action on her own. The characterization of Pendergast has a real modern-day Sherlock Holmes feel to it. He has always had that type of appeal to me, but the last few books have had him able to get out of binds with nearly superhuman strength and abilities. He still has one of those moments in White Fire, but most of the time he is merely a supremely intelligent, totally dominant, impeccably dressed, FBI Special Agent.<br /><br />Preston and Child have written a tightly constructed, very entertaining book that even gives you a \\"long-lost\\" Sherlock Holmes story in the middle. There is a Sir Arthur Conan Doyle and Oscar Wilde connection in the prologue of the book, which continues to pop up though out the story. They have given us a very enjoyable book connecting the true story from 1889 to the fictional novel set in 2013.<br /><br />I give this book 5 Stars out of 5 and a Big Thumbs Up! If you like a good, action thriller, and have a fondness for Sherlock Holmes, then you will love White Fire.<br /><br />I received this Digital Review Copy for free from NetGalley.com.

0452273331|5.0|[[ASIN:0452273331 The Fountainhead]]<br /><br />The hero of Ayn Rand's modern classic, The Fountainhead, is visionary architect Howard Roark. The setting and time is east coast metropolis of the 1930s. The vogue of the New York City Intellectual Elite is conformity to a collectivist ideology - the deification of society as one living, breathing entity. It is a philosophy promoting the concepts of self-less altruism. Conversely, it damns any `selfish,' individualistic ego that may refuse to conform to the `common good of the whole,' one prominent example being Howard Roark.<br /><br />It is obvious to me that Rand is referencing socialism and communism in both of her classics, the other being Atlas Shrugged, published in 1957, but she never uses these two words or any variation thereof. Instead she employs the language and mindset that emanates from those who embrace these ideologies. It is a much more effective way to help us, the readers, to identify a nation that is in transition from personal liberty to mass enslavement. That is why both of Ms. Rand's classic novels have remained perpetual best-sellers from the dates when first published unto this very moment in time. Both remain relevant in A.D. / C.E. 2013.<br /><br />The story begins in the early Depression years when, despite the Art Deco movement, the architectural status quo was still linked to the past; to designs paying homage to ancient Rome and Greece, the Renaissance, to Gothic architecture and traditional British norms. In my opinion, Architect Howard Roark is a type of the great Frank Lloyd Wright, an innovator who dared to be different; to think outside of socially-established parameters. Roark is an unyielding man of genius. He has a vision for the future and will not compromise his `radical' architectural designs for any other man or any amount of money.<br /><br />Once a client signs-off on Roark's design, he must also sign a written affirmation that the building, whether a small house or majestic skyscraper, will not suffer any alteration during its construction; that the client will not give in to public criticism; nor to the peer pressure, which will predictably and inevitably implore him to build something more conventional and less controversial.<br /><br />Throughout the story, Howard Roark valiantly fights an uphill battle. He is condemned for his \\"selfish persistence,\\" his \\"arrogance,\\" his \\"lack of consideration for what is respectable,\\" for his refusal to accept all that is \\"safe, tried and true.\\" Many men of influence attempt to break him, to destroy him but he will not surrender. Roark has total confidence in his own visions. He knows that he is the future; that he will die in battle if necessary to remain faithful to his projected goals.<br /><br />I can personally relate to Roark's struggle because as a semi-retired commercial artist, copywriter and radio production director, I too faced an uphill battle because of my experimental concepts in advertising; ideas that spit in the face of accepted norms. Being merely an employee - one cog in a large machine - I generally lost my battles because I was a servant, not an independent freelancer. In the few instances where my \\"strange ideas\\" were allowed to become print and broadcast realities, I won top awards in the local ad club competition because our judges were generally flown-in from top agencies in New York or Los Angeles but sadly, most of my career has been given to concession.<br /><br />Howard Roark, Architect, epitomizes what I and thousands of other gifted men and women aspire to become - but rarely do.<br /><br />Ayn Rand weaves her Objectivist philosophy into The Fountainhead for reason of inspiring the reader. She demonstrates through her characters how \\"the virtue of selfishness\\" and triumph of the Ego, when personally embraced, can liberate a great mind to realize its full potential - no matter what the odds.<br /><br />If I had been mentally capable of comprehending Ayn Rand's writing style when I was in my late teens searching - as all teenagers do - for an identity, it may have changed the course of my life but as the tired, old clich&eacute; goes: \\"Hindsight is always 20-20.\\"<br /><br />Still at age 66, her two modern classics have given me renewed inspiration. Both have abolished the existential vacuum in my soul. They have brought to a screeching halt my protracted intellectual suicide and given me sound reasons to continue living, thinking, creating.<br /><br />In today's unstable society where young people are being indoctrinated with despair and hopelessness; when my generation in Washington, D.C. is creating an economic mortgage for our children and grandchildren that they will never be able to repay under our current socio-political system, Ayn Rand's The Fountainhead and Atlas Shrugged are must-reads, and re-reads for those who may have forgotten that great civilizations are the product of great minds - the fruit of the few Atlases who set a determined course for their own pursuit of happiness but in the process, also bring major advances to the betterment of all humankind. Let us hope Atlas never does shrug.ng style when I was in my late teens searching - as all teenagers do - for an identity, it may have changed the course of my life but as the tired, old clichÃ© goes: \\"Hindsight is always 20-20.\\"<br /><br />Still at age 66, her two modern classics have given me renewed inspiration. 1476734941|5.0|Here's some background before my review. I'm a 33 year old woman who has NEVER dieted. I have always been able to eat whatever I wanted, whenever I wanted and was very skinny - maybe even too skinny? I'm 5'2.5\\" and weighed 111 lb when I quit smoking after 16 years in April of 2012. I gained 9 lb in the first week - which made me nervous to say the least...was I going to gain 9 lb every week?!?! I stabilized after that, though. I signed up for my first triathlon before I even quit so I was working out really hard and gained another 5 lb. I was OK with my so-called muscle weight. Gaining 14 lb was difficult but I still looked good and knew I was really healthy so I was OK with it. After the triathlon my workouts fell off. I gained a few lb; nothing too drastic. By February of 2013 I had gained 10 - to 135. I still felt OK and looked good so I was not super worried. Then it happened - between March and April I gained 5 lb. I weighed 140 lb?!?! I freaked out, got on myfitness pal, got back to the gym, but continued to gain weight. I was frustrated to say the least. I'd obsess, stop thinking about it, and still gain weight.<br /><br />My mom saw an article about this diet in a fitness magazine and shared it with me in late August. By October, I maxed out at about 148 lb and was seriously losing it. I began thinking about how I used to eat when I was so skinny. It was similar to the fast diet - not on purpose but I'd have days I'd be so busy or stressed, I'd hardly eat at all. The rest of the days I'd eat normal - whatever I wanted. I decided to give it a try. The first fast day (a Thursday) I managed 923 calories. The next (Saturday) was 836. I gradually decreased but usually stay around 600 though the book says 500 for women. I think that doing it more gradually has made it easier and is why I've actually been able to stick to it for the five weeks and I recommend that to people trying this for the first time. You do have to listen to your body. 500 was too low the first week. Gradually, I've become used to eating less and it's not as hard. I now have a routine. There's a salad at the grocery store I love with fat free dressing that is only 300 calories. I don't eat anything in the morning. I like to save my calories for a more substantial meal. I'm totally full after eating it. I have tea in the afternoon to get me through till dinner when I have either two organic eggs and a pita for about 250 calories or a piece of fish and steamed veggies for about the same amount. That's what works for me and it took me a few weeks to figure that out.<br /><br />I did forget to fast two days during these last five weeks (meaning I only fasted one day during week 2 and week 4). From what I can tell on the scale (I weigh myself WAY too often) but I've lost 5 lb - 1 lb per week. I'm so excited! It's the ONLY thing that has actually made the number start to go down. I have another 18 lb to lose. I'm hoping to increase my weight loss to 1.5 lb per week by making sure I stick to the 500 calories and don't skip any fast days. That makes my goal only 12 weeks away! I'll update but I believe it's attainable. I'm not starving myself. I find that I'm not as hungry on my non-fast days. I look at it this way, when I binge out on food, I'm more hungry the next day. The fast works the same in way in reverse. When I refrain from eating so much, I'm not as hungry. Also, I never bought the book. I do love reading reviews though and am sure there is lots of valuable information in it.<br /><br />UPDATE - 11/5/2014<br /><br />I have been doing this diet on and off for the past 13 months. I am down a total of 18 pounds so far and I'm ecstatic. I still have 9 left to lose and they have been stubborn. I keep going up then down. I'm now back finally to my lowest I was two months ago by fasting two days in a row (down about three pounds I've been fluctuating around the last few months) and that seems to be the kick-start I needed. Not easy, mind you...but effective.I am now fasting Monday,Tuesday, & Thursday. I'm hoping to only have to keep this up a few weeks to get down the final 9 pounds and then plan to fast one day per week to maintain my weight and health benefits. I just thought I'd update my review to include this tip in case anyone else gets stuck or hits a plateau. Fasting two days in a row can be challenging. I just get into a zone and stay really busy. Sometimes it's actually easier than two non-consecutive days because I feel less hungry after my first fast day anyway, and a little bit of food fills me up so much quicker. Oh and water, water, water. And I'm a tea drinker so that helps curb the appetite too. Good luck everyone! :)& Thursday. 0375842209|5.0|There are very few times in my life where a historical event really affects me.  History is taught so clinically that the events seem so factual, not human, and almost not relatable.  The two times I have become emotionally involved in the past have been because I read a fictional book that used that setting or event as the background for the story.  The first time this happened was when I read LAMB by Christopher Moore.  The next was today, as I read The Book Thief by Markus Zusak.   There is so much to say about this book that I am having trouble putting it into words.  Markus Zusak did such an incredible job describing what the life of an everyday German was like during the time of Hitler and WWII.  I really had never even thought about the ordinary people.  When you think of Germany in WWII you think about the Jews, Anne Frank, or the Nazi's.  History books just don't talk about how life was, or that there were a lot of people in Germany that didn't agree with the propaganda, but had no choice but to comply with the laws.   The character development was also phenomenal.  It blows my mind.  And when bad things started to happen to the characters as a result of the poverty or air raids it just grips your heart and tears you to pieces.  I think it affects me so much because on a logical level I know that events in the book happened in real life, maybe not exactly like that but there were real innocent people in bomb shelters, and losing family to the war or malnutrition.  In my lifetime I will never experience that kind of reality, but through this book I lived it in my mind and in my heart.   This is the type of book that as you are reading it, you want so badly for the ending to be happy.  But I am glad it isn't.  This way it's more relatable and true to history.  I in fact had to double check that this was a Fictional book and was not based on someone (Liesel's) life story.  I did learn that the author took stories his parents told of Germany and integrated theminto the story, which explains how realistic the book is.   The other significant part of this book is the Narration.  You would expect that the main character (Liesel) to be the Narrator as it is her story.  But I think making Death the narrator and really humanizing him made the book better.  He leaves little insights and tidbits that resonate with the reader.  For he is reluctant and tired, at the same time he is respectful and gentile and invested in one little girl.  For him to be so busy but take time to check in on one human means there is something special about her.  I think this book is one of those that you read as a young adult and then again as an adult when you can read it without having to write a report on analyze it.  This is a must read for both young adults and older adults.  It is heart wrenching and thought provoking.    Check out more YA book reviews and other fun things at [...]

B00F5HWC7W|4.0|It's hard to believe it's been almost a decade since The Killers first burst onto the scene. I remember when Hot Fuss and its singles were everywhere, seemingly coming out of nowhere and surprising all of us with their energetic and passionate performances. This collection celebrates the band's first decade together and it's exactly what you would expect from a basic hits collection. From the big hits like \\"Mr. Brightside\\" and \\"When You Were Young\\" to newer masterpieces like \\"A Dustland Fairytale\\" and \\"Miss Atomic Bomb\\", everything here does a solid job of representing the band's radio singles and popular tunes. The one surprise comes with \\"The Way It Was\\", which was never released as a single but it's a track I've always loved so I can forgive its inclusion here, as well as \\"Be Still\\", which closes the deluxe edition. It's another wonderful track that seemed like an underdog on Battle Born. The two new tracks \\"Shot at the Night\\" and \\"Just Another Girl\\" are both solid and grow on you with every spin. It's really amazing to see how well the songs in this collection have aged. \\"All These Things That I've Done\\", \\"Read My Mind\\", and \\"Human\\" still sound as fresh as they did years ago and The Killers have a knack for writing songs that seem to transcend trends and certain time periods. Direct Hits is certainly a testament to that mentality and to the band's ability to shift their sound from album to album. It's more apparent than ever with this release just how ambitious they are and the drive they maintain to never make the same album twice.<br /><br />That being said, there are a few glaring omissions. The bombastic \\"Bones\\" is sorely absent here, as are \\"The World We Live In\\", \\"Tranquilize\\" (featuring the late Lou Reed) and \\"Here with Me\\".  I understand they had to cut a few tracks but it would have been nice to see these included on the deluxe version. It's also disappointing that diehard fans, aside from the two new songs, don't have much to gain from this. Obviously it's geared toward casual fans and newcomers, which is fine, but including a bonus disc of b-sides or a DVD would have gone a long way toward making this feel more like a more inclusive and complete package. It's a minor complaint but one I suspect many fans will voice.<br /><br />In the end Direct Hits manages to hit most of its targets. For those who want just the basics or an organized introduction to the group then this collection is a good place to start. It's just a bit disappointing to see a lack of bonus content, especially in light of what bands like U2, Keane, and Foo Fighters have done with their respective collections. That would have elevated this release from solid to essential.<br /><br />Their first decade was truly fantastic. B007FEFLTO|4.0|Ken Follett's second novel in the \\"Century Trilogy\\" (following on the heels of \\"Fall of Giants,\\" which focuses on the WWI era) takes our favorite families into the next generation and World War II.  In a novel that spans the 1930s and 1940s over 900-plus pages, Follett has created a page-turner that is yet massive in scope and heft.<br /><br />The Century Trilogy, so far, offers a lot to admire.  Follett's characters span the globe - Welsh, Russian, American, German - and have a magical ability to appear in key yet anonymous roles at pivotal historical events.  Follett's characters witness the rise of Hitler, the Blitz's raids on London, the Russian front, Pearl Harbor, the fall of Berlin, Stalin's near-ouster as de facto tsar, and even the Manhattan Project.  Through it all, Follett keeps events moving quickly, and the characters are just as absorbed in their love lives and marriages (not always the same thing) as they are in the four-power division of Berlin or sussing out spies at Los Alamos.<br /><br />For fans of history, this can be a bit frustrating as major events are given two or three pages.  I find it enjoyable, though, because Follett is not telling the story of Presidents, Prime Ministers, and Generals leading their nations through war, but instead on the impact of titanic events on the everyday people.  Well, perhaps not 'everyday' people, as Follett's characters are given more than their fair share of talent, ambition and dedication.  But they are definitely not the Great Men of the era, even as they rub shoulders with them.<br /><br />But it is refreshing to read the stories of people coping with the hell of the mid-20th century.  Yes, the world nearly tore itself apart, but somehow we made it through, and Follett's point seems to be that humanity survived in large part due to the quiet heroism of everyday people - those who refused to yield when tested (and tested, and tested again).<br /><br />All in all, another genre-defining epic of historical fiction by Mr. Follett.

B00BAXFECK|5.0|The Goldfinch pulls the reader right into the life of its young protagonist Theo via a violent event, a terrorist attack in an art museum, where Theo's mother dies and he steals a painting, a masterpiece. This pivotal event powers the plot, which is credible only through Donna Tartt's brilliant writing. Theo's character is developed through dramatic hardships. He struggles with PTSD and an obsession with a girl who was also damaged in the museum explosion.<br /><br />But it is Theo's obsession with the painting that explores the theme of beauty and the power and purpose of art. Because Ms. Tartt creates her characters so skillfully and builds the story so competently, I was completely invested in her view. The power of the aesthetic experience is understood here. We are led to wonder where meaningful beauty and idolatry intersect.<br /><br />Theo's experience of love is twisted by his neurosis, but the novel's exploration of romantic love, practical pairing versus true love, is universal. Actually, there are many ways that Theo rejects the ordinary and chooses the extreme, even when it's quite destructive. He learns about fate and luck from his gambling father, and forms vague beliefs based on his dramatic experiences. His philosophy of life is understandably grim. But this is a character we root for, and this is a book that I am very happy to have read.
